      <p><b>Sierra Leone</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɛr/: 'err' in 'merry'">ɛr</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>(<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>)/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Sierra_Leone.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/da/En-us-Sierra_Leone.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Sierra Leone.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <small>also</small> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɛər/: 'are' in 'bare'">ɛər</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span>-/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">ɪər</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span>-/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Sierra Leone</b>, informally <b>Salone</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-Salone_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salone-9">[9]</a></sup> is a country on the southwest coast of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> to the southeast and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to the northeast. Sierra Leone has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with a diverse environment ranging from <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> to <a href="/wiki/Rainforests" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainforests">rainforests</a>, a total area of 71,740&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (27,699&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-Sierra_Leone_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sierra_Leone-10">[10]</a></sup> and a population of 7,092,113 as of the 2015 census.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2015_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2015-11">[11]</a></sup> The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>. The country is divided into five administrative regions which are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Districts of Sierra Leone">sixteen districts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:02_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-13">[13]</a></sup> Sierra Leone is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional republic">constitutional republic</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral parliament">unicameral parliament</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Directly_elected" class="mw-redirect" title="Directly elected">directly elected</a> president. Sierra Leone is a <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> majority country at approximately 78%, though with a politically influential <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> minority at about 21%. Muslims and Christians interact very well together and <a href="/wiki/Religious_violence" title="Religious violence">religious violence</a> is extremely rare in the country. All the major Muslim and Christian holidays a officially <a href="/wiki/National_holidays" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="National holidays">national holidays</a> in the country. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone achieved independence from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on 27 April 1961, and Milton Margai became the country's first Prime Minister. Sierra Leone held its first general election as an independent nation on May 27, 1962. <a href="/wiki/Siaka_Stevens" title="Siaka Stevens">Siaka Stevens</a> was democratically elected Prime Minister in 1967, however, once in office, he became increasingly authoritarian during his rule from 1968 to 1985. From 1978 to 1985, Stevens' APC party was the only legal political party in Sierra Leone, and all other political parties were banned. </p>
      <p>The multiparty democratic <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Constitution of Sierra Leone">constitution of Sierra Leone</a> was again adopted in 1991 by President <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Saidu_Momoh" title="Joseph Saidu Momoh">Joseph Saidu Momoh</a>, Stevens' hand-picked choice. From March 23, 1991 to 2002, a group of former Sierra Leone soldiers launched a brutal civil war in a failed attempt to overthrow the Sierra Leone Government. The APC's 24-year rule of Sierra Leone ended on April 29, 1992 in a military coup and a 25-year-old <a href="/wiki/Captain_(armed_forces)" title="Captain (armed forces)">Captain</a> <a href="/wiki/Valentine_Strasser" title="Valentine Strasser">Valentine Strasser</a> ruled the country from 1992 to 1996 in a junta government. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone returned to a democratically elected government when the <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">military junta</a> under <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">Brigadier</a> <a href="/wiki/Julius_Maada_Bio" title="Julius Maada Bio">Julius Maada Bio</a> handed the presidency to <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">Sierra Leone People's Party</a> (SLPP) after his victory in the 1996 election. However, the Sierra Leone military overthrew President Kabbah in a coup on May 25, 1997, A coalition of West African <a href="/wiki/ECOWAS" class="mw-redirect" title="ECOWAS">ECOWAS</a> armed forces led by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> reinstated President Kabbah in February 1998. In January 2002, President Kabbah officially announced the end of the civil war. Sierra Leone has uninterrupted democratic government from 1998 to the present day. </p>
      <p>Sixteen ethnic groups inhabit Sierra Leone, the two largest and most influential being the <a href="/wiki/Temne_people" title="Temne people">Temne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a> peoples. About 2% of the country's population are <a href="/wiki/Krio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Krio people">Krio</a>, descendants of freed <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> slaves. English is the official language used in schools and government administration; however, <a href="/wiki/Krio_language" title="Krio language">Krio</a> is the most widely spoken language across Sierra Leone, spoken by 97% of the country's population. Sierra Leone is very rich in natural resources, especially <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aluminum" class="mw-redirect" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a>. The country is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS), <a href="/wiki/Mano_River_Union" title="Mano River Union">Mano River Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The country takes its name from the <a href="/wiki/Lion_Mountains" title="Lion Mountains">Lion Mountains</a> near Freetown. Originally named <i>Serra Leoa</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for "Lioness Mountains") by Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Sintra" title="Pedro de Sintra">Pedro de Sintra</a> in 1462, the modern name is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> spelling, which was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venetian</a> explorer <a href="/wiki/Alvise_Cadamosto" title="Alvise Cadamosto">Alvise Cadamosto</a> and subsequently copied by other European <a href="/wiki/Cartography" title="Cartography">mapmakers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_Sierra_Leone">History of Sierra Leone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History of Sierra Leone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Sierra_Leone" title="History of Sierra Leone">History of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Governor_John_Thomas%27s_house_in_Sierra_Leone,_mid-17th_century,_artist%27s_recreation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Houses at Sierra-Leone (May 1853, X, p.55)<sup id="cite_ref-Juvenile1853_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juvenile1853-15">[15]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Archaeological finds show that Sierra Leone has been inhabited continuously for at least 2,500 years,<sup id="cite_ref-Culture_of_Sierra_Leone_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Culture_of_Sierra_Leone-16">[16]</a></sup> populated successively by societies who migrated from other parts of Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Sierra_Leone_History_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sierra_Leone_History-17">[17]</a></sup> The use of iron was adopted by the 9th century, and by 1000 AD, agriculture was being practised along the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-Sierra_Leone_-_History_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sierra_Leone_-_History-18">[18]</a></sup> Over time, the climate changed considerably, altering boundaries between different ecological zones, affecting migration and conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-brooks_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brooks-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone's dense tropical rainforest and swampy environment was considered impenetrable; it was also host to the <a href="/wiki/Tsetse_fly" title="Tsetse fly">tsetse fly</a>, which carried a disease fatal to horses and the <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">zebu</a> cattle used by the <a href="/wiki/Mande_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mande people">Mande people</a>. This environment protected its people from conquest by the Mande and other African empires,<sup id="cite_ref-brooks_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brooks-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-protected_from_influence_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-protected_from_influence-20">[20]</a></sup> and limited the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was introduced by <a href="/wiki/Sosso_Empire" title="Sosso Empire">Susu</a> traders, merchants and migrants from the north and east, becoming widely adopted in the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforest_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforest-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_trading">European trading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European trading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>European contacts within Sierra Leone were among the first in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> in the 15th century. In 1462, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Sintra" title="Pedro de Sintra">Pedro de Sintra</a> mapped the hills surrounding what is now Freetown Harbour, naming the shaped formation <i>Serra da Leoa</i> or "Serra Leoa" (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for <a href="/wiki/Lioness_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Lioness Mountains">Lioness Mountains</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-22">[22]</a></sup> The Spanish rendering of this geographic formation is <i>Sierra Leona</i>, which later was adapted and, misspelled, became the country's current name. Although according to the <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a> C. Magbaily Fyle this could have been a misinterpretation of historians: according to him, there has been evidence of travellers calling the region <i>Serra Lyoa</i> well before 1462, the year when Sintra first arrived. This would imply that the identity of the person who named Sierra Leone is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Soon after Sintra's expedition, Portuguese traders arrived at the harbour. By 1495 they had built a fortified <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading post</a> on the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-LeVert_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeVert-24">[24]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> also set up trade here, and each nation used Sierra Leone as a trading point for <a href="/wiki/Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave">slaves</a> brought by African traders from interior areas undergoing wars and conflicts over territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Sibthorpe_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sibthorpe-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1562, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> initiated the <a href="/wiki/Triangle_Trade" class="mw-redirect" title="Triangle Trade">Triangle Trade</a> when admiral <a href="/wiki/John_Hawkins_(naval_commander)" title="John Hawkins (naval commander)">Sir John Hawkins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> transported 300 enslaved Africans – acquired "by the sword and partly by other means" – to the Spanish colony of <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a> on <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> area of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> islands, where he sold them.<sup id="cite_ref-Sir_John_Hawkins_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sir_John_Hawkins-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_colonies">Early colonies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early colonies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the late 18th century, many African-Americans claimed the protection of the <a href="/wiki/British_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="British Crown">British Crown</a>. There were thousands of these <a href="/wiki/Black_Loyalists" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Loyalists">Black Loyalists</a>, people of African descent who joined the British military forces during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Many of these <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Loyalists</a> had been slaves who escaped to join the British, lured by promises of freedom (<a href="/wiki/Emancipation" title="Emancipation">emancipation</a>). The official documentation known as the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Negroes" title="Book of Negroes">Book of Negroes</a> lists thousands of freed slaves whom the British evacuated from the nascent United States and resettled in colonies elsewhere in <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> (north to Canada, or south to the West Indies). </p>
      <p>In 1787 the British Crown founded a settlement in Sierra Leone in what was called the "<a href="/wiki/Province_of_Freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Province of Freedom">Province of Freedom</a>". It intended to resettle some of the "<a href="/wiki/Black_Poor" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Poor">Black Poor</a> of London", some of whom were African-Americans freed by the British during the war. About 400 blacks and 60 whites reached Sierra Leone on 15 May 1787. The group also included some <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indians</a> of African descent from London. After they established <a href="/wiki/Granville_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Granville Town">Granville Town</a>, most of the first group of colonists died, owing to disease and warfare with the indigenous African peoples (<a href="/wiki/Temne_people" title="Temne people">Temne</a>), who resisted their encroachment. The 64&nbsp;remaining colonists established a second Granville Town.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, more than 3,000 Black Loyalists had also been settled in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, where they were finally granted land. They founded <a href="/wiki/Birchtown,_Nova_Scotia" title="Birchtown, Nova Scotia">Birchtown, Nova Scotia</a>, but faced harsh winters and racial discrimination from nearby <a href="/wiki/Shelburne,_Nova_Scotia" title="Shelburne, Nova Scotia">Shelburne, Nova Scotia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Peters_(black_leader)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Peters (black leader)">Thomas Peters</a> pressed British authorities for relief and more aid; together with British abolitionist <a href="/wiki/John_Clarkson_(abolitionist)" title="John Clarkson (abolitionist)">John Clarkson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Company" title="Sierra Leone Company">Sierra Leone Company</a> was established to relocate Black Loyalists who wanted to take their chances in West Africa. In 1792 nearly 1200&nbsp;persons from Nova Scotia crossed the Atlantic to build the second (and only permanent) Colony of Sierra Leone and the settlement of <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a> on 11 March 1792. In Sierra Leone they were called the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotian_Settlers" title="Nova Scotian Settlers">Nova Scotian Settlers</a>, the <i>Nova Scotians</i>, or the <i>Settlers</i>. </p>
      <p>The Settlers built Freetown in the styles they knew from their lives in the <a href="/wiki/American_South" class="mw-redirect" title="American South">American South</a>; they also continued American fashion and American manners. In addition, many continued to practise <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a> in Freetown. Black settlers in Sierra Leone enjoyed much more autonomy in that they were more politically engaged. Black immigrants elected different levels of political representatives, 'tithingmen', who represented each dozen settlers, and 'hundreders' who represented larger amounts. This sort of representation was not available in Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The initial process of society-building in Freetown, however, was a harsh struggle. The Crown did not supply enough basic supplies and provisions, and the Settlers were continually threatened by illegal slave trading and the risk of re-enslavement.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In the 1790s, the Settlers, including adult women, voted for the first time in elections.<sup id="cite_ref-economist_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist-32">[32]</a></sup> The Sierra Leone Company, controlled by London investors, refused to allow the settlers to take <a href="/wiki/Fee_simple" title="Fee simple">freehold</a> of the land. In 1799 some of the settlers revolted. The Crown subdued the revolt by bringing in forces of more than 500&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Maroons" title="Jamaican Maroons">Jamaican Maroons</a>, whom they transported from <a href="/wiki/Cudjoe%27s_Town_(Trelawny_Town)" title="Cudjoe's Town (Trelawny Town)">Cudjoe's Town (Trelawny Town)</a> via Nova Scotia in 1800. Led by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Montague_James" title="Montague James">Montague James</a>, the Maroons helped the colonial forces to put down the revolt, and in the process the <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Maroons_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Jamaican Maroons in Sierra Leone">Jamaican Maroons in Sierra Leone</a> secured the best houses and farms.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 January 1808, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ludlam_(colonialist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Ludlam (colonialist)">Thomas Ludlam</a>, the Governor of the Sierra Leone Company and a leading abolitionist, surrendered the company's charter. This ended its 16&nbsp;years of running the Colony. The British Crown reorganised the Sierra Leone Company as the <a href="/wiki/African_Institution" title="African Institution">African Institution</a>; it was directed to improve the local economy. Its members represented both British who hoped to inspire local entrepreneurs and those with interest in the Macauley &amp; Babington Company, which held the (British) monopoly on Sierra Leone trade.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At about the same time (following the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Trade_Act_1807" title="Slave Trade Act 1807">abolition of the slave trade in 1807</a>), British crews delivered thousands of formerly enslaved Africans to Freetown, after liberating them from illegal slave ships. These Liberated Africans or <i><a href="/wiki/Recaptives" class="mw-redirect" title="Recaptives">recaptives</a></i> were sold for $20 a head as apprentices to the white settlers, Nova Scotian Settlers, and the Jamaican Maroons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some of the recaptives who were not sold as apprentices were forced to join the Navy. Many recaptives were treated poorly and even abused because some of the original settlers considered them their property. Cut off from their various homelands and traditions, the Liberated Africans were forced to assimilate to the Western styles of Settlers and Maroons. For example, some of the recaptives were forced to change their name to a more Western sounding one. Though some people happily embraced these changes because they considered it as being part of the community, some were not happy with these changes and wanted to keep their own identity. Many recaptives were so unhappy that they risked the possibility of being sold back into slavery by leaving Sierra Leone and going back to their original villages.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> They built a flourishing trade in flowers and beads on the West African coast. </p>
      <p>These returned Africans were from many areas of Africa, but principally the west coast. During the 19th century, freed black Americans, some <a href="/wiki/Americo_Liberian" class="mw-redirect" title="Americo Liberian">Americo Liberian</a> 'refugees', and particularly West Indians, also immigrated and settled in Freetown. Together these peoples created a new creole ethnicity called the <a href="/wiki/Krio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Krio people">Krio people</a> (initially called Creoles) and a trading language, <a href="/wiki/Krio_language" title="Krio language">Krio</a>, which became commonly used among many of the ethnicities in the country. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Colonial_era_.281800.E2.80.931961.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era_(1800–1961)">Colonial era (1800–1961)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Colonial era (1800–1961)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Colony_and_Protectorate" title="Sierra Leone Colony and Protectorate">Sierra Leone Colony and Protectorate</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The settlement of Sierra Leone in the 1800s was unique in that the population was composed of displaced Africans who were brought to the colony after the British abolition of the slave trade in 1807. Upon arrival in Sierra Leone, each "recaptive" was given a registration number, and information on their physical qualities would be entered into the Register of Liberated Africans. However, oftentimes the documentation would be overwhelmingly subjective and would result in inaccurate entries, making them difficult to track. In addition, differences between the Register of Liberated Africans of 1808 and the List of Captured Negroes of 1812 (which emulated the 1808 document) revealed some disparities in the entries of the recaptives, specifically in the names; many recaptives decided to change their given names to more <a href="/wiki/Anglicised" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicised">anglicised</a> versions which contributed to the difficulty in tracking them after they arrived in Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p> According to the British Act for the Abolition of the Slave Trade in 1807, the recaptives could be subject to apprenticeships led by British colonists in Sierra Leone and the males enlisted into the Army or Navy. In many instances, the recaptives who were assigned to apprenticeships were sold for $20, giving the apprenticeship system qualities similar to slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-Schwartz_2012_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz_2012-36">[36]</a></sup> It is documented that the recaptive apprentices were unpaid and the settlers who they were appointed to had devices which could be used to discipline them, namely sticks. According to Suzanne Schwartz, a historian on colonial Sierra Leone, in June 1808 a group of 21 men and women ran away to the nearby native settlement of Robiss and upon recapture were imprisoned by the settlers in Sierra Leone, thus contributing to the slavery-like qualities of the apprenticeship system.<sup id="cite_ref-Schwartz_2012_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schwartz_2012-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bureh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bai_Bureh.jpg/200px-Bai_Bureh.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bai_Bureh.jpg/300px-Bai_Bureh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Bai_Bureh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="396" data-file-height="525"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bureh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bai_Bureh" title="Bai Bureh">Bai Bureh</a>, Temne leader of the <a href="/wiki/Hut_Tax_War_of_1898" title="Hut Tax War of 1898">Hut Tax War of 1898</a> against British rule
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the early 19th century, Freetown served as the residence of the British colonial governor of the region, who also administered the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(British_colony)" title="Gold Coast (British colony)">Gold Coast</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a> settlements. Sierra Leone developed as the educational centre of British West Africa. The British established <a href="/wiki/Fourah_Bay_College" title="Fourah Bay College">Fourah Bay College</a> here in 1827, which rapidly became a magnet for English-speaking Africans on the West Coast. For more than a century, it was the only European-style university in western <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bureh_(1898).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg/220px-Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg/330px-Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg/440px-Bai_Bureh_%281898%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="771" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bai_Bureh_(1898).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Temne leader Bai Bureh seen here in 1898 after his surrender, sitting relaxed in his traditional dress with a handkerchief in his hands, while a Sierra Leonean <a href="/wiki/Royal_West_African_Frontier_Force" title="Royal West African Frontier Force">Royal West African Frontier</a> soldier stands guard next to him
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The British interacted mostly with the Krios in Freetown, who did most of the trading with the indigenous peoples of the interior. In addition, educated Krios held numerous positions in the colonial government, giving them status and well-paying positions. Following the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> of 1884–1885, the UK decided that it needed to establish more dominion over the inland areas, to satisfy what was described by the European powers as "effective occupation" of territories. In 1896 it annexed these areas, declaring them the Sierra Leone Protectorate.<sup id="cite_ref-harris40_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harris40-37">[37]</a></sup> With this change, the British began to expand their administration in the region, recruiting British citizens to posts, and pushing Krios out of positions in government and even the desirable residential areas in Freetown.<sup id="cite_ref-harris40_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harris40-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the British annexation to Sierra Leone, there were several chiefs in the Northern and Southern part of the country who were also resisting the hut tax war but they used diplomacy to achieve their goal. To the north, from 1820 to 1906 there was a Limba chief named Almamy Suluku who ruled his territory for many years, fighting different tribes to protect his territory, while at the same time using diplomacy to trick the protectorate and sending fighters to assist Bai Bureh. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html">http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html</a>. Another prominent figure in Sierra Leone history is Bai Sherbro (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1830–1912</span>). Bai Sherbro was a chief and warrior in Bonte Island, which is in the southwestern part of the country. He, like Bai Bureh, exercised resistance to the British. Bai Sherbro also sent fighters to Bai Bureh’s camp to help him fight against the British. Bai Sherbro was influential and powerful, so the British greatly feared him. Bai Sherbro was subsequently captured, and along with Bai Bureh exiled to the Gold Coast, which is now modern day Ghana. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html">http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html</a>. Nyagua, (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1842–1906</span>), also known as the tracking king, was a fierce King who captured many districts and many came to join him for protection. Nyagua was also resistant to the British cause. However, Nyagua, realizing that he lacked sufficient strength, attempted to use diplomacy. At the same time, he sent warriors to assist Bai Bureh to fight against the British. The British later captured Nyagua, and he was also exiled to the Gold Coast. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html">http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html</a>. Madam Yoko, (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1849–1906</span>) was a brilliant woman of culture and ambition. She employed her capacity for friendly communications to persuade the British to give her control of the Kpaa Mende chiefdom. She used diplomacy to communicate with many local chiefs who did not trust her friendship with the British. Because Madam Yoko supported the British, some sub-chiefs rebelled, causing Yoko to take refuge in the police barracks. For her loyalty, she was awarded a silver medal by Queen Victoria. Until 1906 Madam Yoko ruled as a paramount chief in the new British Protectorate. Sadly, it appears that she committed suicide at the age of fifty-five, perhaps due to the loss of support from her own people. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html">http://www.sierra-leone.org/Heroes/heroes5.html</a>. </p>
      <p>In addition, the British annexation of the Protectorate interfered with the sovereignty of indigenous chiefs. They designated chiefs as units of local government, rather than dealing with them individually as had been the previous practice. They did not maintain relationships even with longtime allies, such as <a href="/wiki/Bai_Bureh" title="Bai Bureh">Bai Bureh</a>, chief of Kasseh, a community on the Small Scarcies River. He was later unfairly portrayed as a prime instigator of the Hut Tax war in 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-abraham_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abraham-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Colonel Frederic Cardew, military governor of the Protectorate, in 1898 established a new tax on dwellings and demanded that the chiefs use their peoples to maintain roads. The taxes were often higher than the value of the dwellings, and 24 chiefs signed a petition to Cardew, stating how destructive this was; their people could not afford to take time off from their subsistence agriculture. They resisted payment of taxes. Tensions over the new colonial requirements, and the administration's suspicions towards the chiefs, led to the <a href="/wiki/Hut_Tax_War_of_1898" title="Hut Tax War of 1898">Hut Tax war of 1898</a>, also called the Temne-Mende War. The British fired first. The Northern front of majority Temne people was led by <a href="/wiki/Bai_Bureh" title="Bai Bureh">Bai Bureh</a>. The Southern front, consisting mostly of <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende people</a>, entered the conflict somewhat later for other reasons. </p>
      <p>For several months, Bureh's fighters had the advantage over the vastly more powerful British forces, but the British troops and Bureh's warriors suffered hundreds of fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Bai Bureh finally surrendered on 11 November 1898 to end the destruction of his people's territory and dwellings. Although the British government recommended leniency, Cardew insisted on sending the chief and two allies into <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exile</a> in the Gold Coast;<sup id="cite_ref-abraham_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abraham-38">[38]</a></sup> his government hanged 96 of the chief's warriors. Bai Bureh was allowed to return in 1905, when he resumed his chieftaincy of Kasseh.<sup id="cite_ref-abraham_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abraham-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SierraLeoneP016.tiff" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/SierraLeoneP016.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-SierraLeoneP016.tiff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/SierraLeoneP016.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-SierraLeoneP016.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/SierraLeoneP016.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-SierraLeoneP016.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3187" data-file-height="2016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SierraLeoneP016.tiff" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Moa River Bridge, Sierra Leone. <a href="/wiki/Alphonso_Lisk-Carew" title="Alphonso Lisk-Carew">Lisk-Carew Brothers</a>, Freetown, Sierra Leone
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown,_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg/220px-British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg/330px-British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg/440px-British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown%2C_1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3067" data-file-height="1774"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:British_Expeditionary_Force_in_Freetown,_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British <a href="/wiki/West_Africa_Campaign_(World_War_I)" class="mw-redirect" title="West Africa Campaign (World War I)">West African Campaign</a> troops in Freetown, 1914–1916. Published caption: "British expeditionary force preparing to embark at Freetown to attack the <a href="/wiki/German_Cameroons" class="mw-redirect" title="German Cameroons">German Cameroons</a>, the main object of the attack being the port of <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Duala</a>. Auxiliary native troops were freely used in African warfare."
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg/220px-The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg/330px-The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg/440px-The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Navy_during_the_Second_World_War_A24465.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>African Naval ratings march past the Governor of Sierra Leone, Hubert Stevenson.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The defeat of the Temne and Mende in the Hut Tax war ended mass resistance to the Protectorate and colonial government, but intermittent rioting and labour unrest continued throughout the colonial period. Riots in 1955 and 1956 involved "many tens of thousands" of Sierra Leonians in the protectorate.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Domestic <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">slavery</a>, which continued to be practised by local African elites, was abolished in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A notable event in 1935 was the granting of a monopoly on mineral mining to the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Selection_Trust" title="Sierra Leone Selection Trust">Sierra Leone Selection Trust</a>, run by <a href="/wiki/De_Beers" title="De Beers">De Beers</a>. The monopoly was scheduled to last 98 years. Mining of diamonds in the east and other minerals expanded, drawing labourers there from other parts of the country. </p>
      <p>In 1924, the UK government divided Sierra Leone into a Colony and a Protectorate, with different political systems constitutionally defined for each. The Colony was Freetown and its coastal area; the Protectorate was defined as the hinterland areas dominated by local chiefs. Antagonism between the two entities escalated to a heated debate in 1947, when proposals were introduced to provide for a single political system for both the Colony and the Protectorate. Most of the proposals came from leaders of the Protectorate, whose population far outnumbered that in the colony. The Krios, led by <a href="/wiki/I._T._A._Wallace-Johnson" title="I. T. A. Wallace-Johnson">Isaac Wallace-Johnson</a>, opposed the proposals, as they would have resulted in reducing the political power of the Krios in the Colony. </p>
      <p>In 1951, educated protectorate leaders from different groups, including <a href="/wiki/Sir" title="Sir">Sir</a> <a href="/wiki/Milton_Margai" title="Milton Margai">Milton Margai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamina_Sankoh" title="Lamina Sankoh">Lamina Sankoh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siaka_Stevens" title="Siaka Stevens">Siaka Stevens</a>, Mohamed Sanusi Mustapha, <a href="/wiki/John_Karefa-Smart" title="John Karefa-Smart">John Karefa-Smart</a>, Kande Bureh, Sir <a href="/wiki/Albert_Margai" title="Albert Margai">Albert Margai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amadu_Wurie" title="Amadu Wurie">Amadu Wurie</a> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Banja_Tejan-Sie" title="Banja Tejan-Sie">Banja Tejan-Sie</a> joined together with the powerful <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chiefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramount chiefs">paramount chiefs</a> in the protectorate to form the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">Sierra Leone People's Party</a> or SLPP as the party of the protectorate. The SLPP leadership, led by Sir Milton Margai, negotiated with the British and the educated Krio-dominated colony based in Freetown to achieve independence.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Owing to the astute politics of Milton Margai of the <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a>, the educated Protectorate elite was won over to join forces with the <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chiefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramount chiefs">paramount chiefs</a> in the face of Krio intransigence. Later, Margai used the same skills to win over opposition leaders and moderate Krio elements to achieve independence from the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In November 1951, Margai oversaw the drafting of a new constitution, which united the separate Colonial and Protectorate legislatures and provided a framework for <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-advocate_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-advocate-44">[44]</a></sup> In 1953, Sierra Leone was granted local ministerial powers and Margai was elected <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister">Chief Minister</a> of Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-advocate_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-advocate-44">[44]</a></sup> The new constitution ensured Sierra Leone a parliamentary system within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-advocate_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-advocate-44">[44]</a></sup> In May 1957, Sierra Leone held its first parliamentary election. The SLPP, which was then the most popular political party in the colony of Sierra Leone as well as being supported by the powerful paramount chiefs in the provinces, won the most seats in Parliament and Margai was re-elected as Chief Minister by a landslide. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960_Independence_Conference">1960 Independence Conference</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1960 Independence Conference">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 20 April 1960, Milton Margai led a 24-member Sierra Leonean delegation at constitutional conferences that were held with the Government of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and British Colonial Secretary <a href="/wiki/Iain_Macleod" title="Iain Macleod">Iain Macleod</a> in negotiations for independence held in London.<sup id="cite_ref-Murtala_Mohammed_Kamara_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murtala_Mohammed_Kamara-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Momoh_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Momoh-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On the conclusion of talks in London on 4 May 1960, the United Kingdom agreed to grant Sierra Leone independence on 27 April 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-Murtala_Mohammed_Kamara_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murtala_Mohammed_Kamara-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Momoh_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Momoh-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281961.29_and_Margai_Administration_.281961.E2.80.931964.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1961)_and_Margai_Administration_(1961–1964)">Independence (1961) and Margai Administration (1961–1964)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence (1961) and Margai Administration (1961–1964)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 27 April 1961, Sir Milton Margai led Sierra Leone to independence from Great Britain and became the country's first Prime Minister. Thousands of Sierra Leoneans took to the streets in celebration. The Dominion of Sierra Leone retained a parliamentary system of government and was a member of the Commonwealth of Nations. The leader of the main opposition <a href="/wiki/All_People%27s_Congress" title="All People's Congress">All People's Congress</a> (APC), Siaka Stevens, along with Isaac Wallace-Johnson, another outspoken critic of the SLPP government, were arrested and placed under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> in Freetown, along with sixteen others charged with disrupting the independence celebration.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 1962, Sierra Leone held its <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_general_election,_1962" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leonean general election, 1962">first general election</a> as an independent nation. The <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">Sierra Leone People's Party</a> (SLPP) won a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> of seats in parliament, and Milton Margai was re-elected as prime minister. </p>
      <p>Margai was very popular among Sierra Leoneans during his time in power, most known for his self-effacement. He was neither corrupt nor did he make a lavish display of his power or status.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> He based the government on the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> and the separation of powers, with multiparty political institutions and fairly viable representative structures. Margai used his conservative ideology to lead Sierra Leone without much strife. He appointed government officials to represent various ethnic groups. Margai employed a brokerage style of politics, by sharing political power among political parties and interest groups; and with the powerful paramount chiefs in the provinces, most of whom were key allies of his government.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Final_years_of_democracy_.281964.E2.80.931967.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_years_of_democracy_(1964–1967)">Final years of democracy (1964–1967)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Final years of democracy (1964–1967)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Upon Milton Margai's unexpected death in 1964, his <a href="/wiki/Half-brother" class="mw-redirect" title="Half-brother">half-brother</a>, Sir <a href="/wiki/Albert_Margai" title="Albert Margai">Albert Margai</a>, was appointed as Prime Minister by parliament. Sir Albert's leadership was briefly challenged by Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Karefa-Smart" title="John Karefa-Smart">John Karefa-Smart</a>, who questioned Sir Albert's succession to the SLPP leadership position. Karefa-Smart led a prominent small minority faction within the SLPP party in opposition of Albert Margai as Prime Minister. However, Karefa-Smart failed to receive strong support within the SLPP and the SLPP dominated members of parliament in his attempt to have Albert Margai stripped of his position as the leader of the SLPP and prime minister of the country. The large majority of SLPP members backed Albert Margai over Karefa-Smart. Soon after Albert Margai was sworn in as Prime Minister, he dismissed several senior government officials who had served under his elder brother Milton's government, viewing them as a threat to his administration, including Karefa-Smart. </p>
      <p>Sir Albert resorted to increasingly <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a> actions in response to protests and enacted several laws against the opposition <a href="/wiki/All_People%27s_Congress" title="All People's Congress">All People's Congress</a> (APC), whilst attempting to establish a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Sir Albert was opposed to the colonial legacy of allowing executive powers to the Paramount Chiefs, many of whom had been key allies of his late brother Sir Milton. Accordingly, they began to consider Sir Albert a threat to the ruling houses across the country. Margai appointed many non-Creoles to the country's <a href="/wiki/Civil_service" title="Civil service">civil service</a> in <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, in an overall diversification of the civil service in the capital, which had been dominated by members of the Creole ethnic group. As a result, Albert Margai became unpopular in the Creole community, many of whom had supported Sir Milton. Margai was accused of favouring members of his own Mende ethnic group for prominent positions. </p>
      <p>In 1967, riots broke out in Freetown against Margai's policies; in response he declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> across the country. Sir Albert was accused of corruption and of a policy of <a href="/wiki/Affirmative_action" title="Affirmative action">affirmative action</a> in favour of his own <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a> ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Although possessing the full backing of the country's security forces, he called for free and fair elections. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Military_coups_.281967.E2.80.931968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_coups_(1967–1968)">Military coups (1967–1968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Military coups (1967–1968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The APC, with its leader <a href="/wiki/Siaka_Stevens" title="Siaka Stevens">Siaka Stevens</a>, narrowly won a small majority of seats in Parliament over the SLPP in a closely contested <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_general_election,_1967" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leonean general election, 1967">1967 general election</a>. Stevens was sworn in as Prime Minister on 21 March 1967. </p>
      <p>Within hours after taking office, Stevens was ousted in a bloodless <a href="/wiki/Military_coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Military coup">military coup</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Brigadier General">Brigadier General</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Lansana" title="David Lansana">David Lansana</a>, the commander of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Sierra_Leone_Armed_Forces" title="Republic of Sierra Leone Armed Forces">Sierra Leone Armed Forces</a>. He was a close ally of Albert Margai, who had appointed him to the position in 1964. Lansana placed Stevens under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> in Freetown and insisted that the determination of Prime Minister should await the election of the tribal representatives to the House. Upon his release, Stevens went into exile in <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>. </p>
      <p>On 23 March 1967, a group of military officers in the Sierra Leone Army led by Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Juxon-Smith" title="Andrew Juxon-Smith">Andrew Juxon-Smith</a>, overrode this action by a coup d'état; they seized control of the government, arresting Lansana, and suspending the constitution. The group set up the <a href="/wiki/National_Reformation_Council" title="National Reformation Council">National Reformation Council</a> (NRC), with Andrew Juxon-Smith as its chairman and Head of State of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 18 April 1968 a group of low ranking soldiers in the Sierra Leone Army who called themselves the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-Corruption_Revolutionary_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anti-Corruption Revolutionary Movement (page does not exist)">Anti-Corruption Revolutionary Movement</a> (ACRM), led by Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/John_Amadu_Bangura" title="John Amadu Bangura">John Amadu Bangura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergeants%27_Coup_(Sierra_Leone)" title="Sergeants' Coup (Sierra Leone)">overthrew</a> the NRC <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">junta</a>. The ACRM junta arrested many senior NRC members. They reinstated the constitution and returned power to Stevens, who at last assumed the office of Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="One-party_state_.281968.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="One-party_state_(1968–1991)">One-party state (1968–1991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: One-party state (1968–1991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg/300px-All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg/450px-All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg/600px-All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="733"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:All_People%27s_Congress_political_rally_Sierra_Leone_1968.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An <a href="/wiki/All_People%27s_Congress" title="All People's Congress">APC</a> political rally in the northern town of <a href="/wiki/Kabala,_Sierra_Leone" title="Kabala, Sierra Leone">Kabala</a> outside the home of supporters of the rival <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">SLPP</a> in 1968
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Stevens assumed power again in 1968 with a great deal of hope and ambition.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Much trust was placed upon him as he championed multiparty politics. Stevens had campaigned on a platform of bringing the tribes together under <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> principles. During his first decade or so in power, Stevens renegotiated some of what he called "useless prefinanced schemes" contracted by his predecessors, both Albert Margai of the SLPP and Juxon-Smith of the NRC. Some of these policies by the SLPP and the NRC were said to have left the country in an economically deprived state.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Stevens reorganised the country's oil refinery, the government-owned Cape Sierra Hotel, and a cement factory.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> He cancelled Juxon-Smith's construction of a church and mosque on the grounds of Victoria Park (since mid 2017 <i>Freetown Amusement Park</i>). Stevens began efforts that would later bridge the distance between the provinces and the city. Roads and hospitals were constructed in the provinces, and Paramount Chiefs and provincial peoples became a prominent force in Freetown. </p>
      <p>Under pressure of several coup attempts, real or perceived, Stevens' rule grew more and more <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian">authoritarian</a>, and his relationship with some of his ardent supporters deteriorated. He removed the SLPP party from competitive politics in general elections, some believed, through the use of violence and intimidation. To maintain the support of the military, Stevens retained the popular John Amadu Bangura as head of the Sierra Leone Armed Forces. </p>
      <p>After the return to civilian rule, by-elections were held (beginning in autumn 1968) and an all-APC cabinet was appointed. Calm was not completely restored. In November 1968, unrest in the provinces led Stevens to declare a state of emergency across the country. Many senior officers in the Sierra Leone Army were greatly disappointed with Stevens' policies and his handling of the Sierra Leone Military, but none could confront Stevens. Brigadier General Bangura, who had reinstated Stevens as Prime Minister, was widely considered the only person who could control Stevens. The army was devoted to Bangura, and this made him potentially dangerous to Stevens. In January 1970, Bangura was arrested and charged with <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(crime)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracy (crime)">conspiracy</a> and plotting to commit a coup against the Stevens government. After a trial that lasted a few months, Bangura was <a href="/wiki/Convicted" class="mw-redirect" title="Convicted">convicted</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">sentenced to death</a>. On 29 March 1970, Brigadier Bangura was executed by hanging in Freetown. </p>
      <p>After the execution of Bangura, a group of soldiers loyal to the executed general held a <a href="/wiki/Mutiny" title="Mutiny">mutiny</a> in Freetown and other parts of the country in opposition to Stevens' government. Dozens of soldiers were arrested and <a href="/wiki/Convicted" class="mw-redirect" title="Convicted">convicted</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Court_martial" class="mw-redirect" title="Court martial">court martial</a> in Freetown for their participation in the mutiny against the president. Among the soldiers arrested was a little-known army <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">Corporal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foday_Sankoh" title="Foday Sankoh">Foday Sankoh</a>, a strong Bangura supporter. Corporal Sankoh was convicted and jailed for seven years at the Pademba Road Prison in Freetown. </p>
      <p>In April 1971, a new republican constitution was adopted under which Stevens became president. In the 1972 by-elections, the opposition SLPP complained of intimidation and procedural obstruction by the APC and militia. These problems became so severe that the SLPP boycotted the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_general_election,_1973" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leonean general election, 1973">1973 general election</a>; as a result the APC won 84 of the 85 elected seats.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An alleged plot to overthrow president Stevens failed in 1974 and its leaders were executed. In mid-1974, Guinean soldiers, as requested by Stevens, were stationed in the country to help maintain his hold on power, as Stevens was a close ally of then-Guinean president <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Sekou_Toure" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmed Sekou Toure">Ahmed Sekou Toure</a>. In March 1976, Stevens was elected without opposition for a second five-year term as president. On 19 July 1975, 14 senior army and government officials, including David Lansana, former cabinet minister Mohamed Sorie Forna (father of writer <a href="/wiki/Aminatta_Forna" title="Aminatta Forna">Aminatta Forna</a>), Brigadier General Ibrahim Bash Taqi and Lieutenant Habib Lansana Kamara were executed after being convicted of attempting a coup to topple president Stevens' government. </p>
      <p>In 1977, a nationwide student demonstration against the government disrupted Sierra Leone politics. The demonstration was quickly put down by the army and Stevens' own personal Special Security Division (SSD), a heavily armed paramilitary force he had created to protect him and maintain his hold on power.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> SSD officers were very loyal to Stevens and were deployed across Sierra Leone to put down any rebellion or protest against Stevens' government. <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_parliamentary_election,_1977" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leonean parliamentary election, 1977">A general election</a> was called later that year in which corruption was again endemic; the APC won 74 seats and the SLPP 15. In 1978, the APC-dominant parliament approved a new constitution making the country a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>. The 1978 constitution made the APC the only legal political party in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-Gberie_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gberie-55">[55]</a></sup> This move led to another major demonstration against the government in many parts of the country, but it was also put down by the army and Stevens' SSD force. </p>
      <p>Stevens is generally criticised for dictatorial methods and government corruption, but on a positive note, he kept the country stable and from collapsing into civil war. He created several government institutions that are still in use today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Stevens also reduced ethnic polarisation in government by incorporating members of various ethnic groups into his all-dominant APC government. </p>
      <p>Siaka Stevens retired from politics in November 1985 after being in power for eighteen years. The APC named a new presidential candidate to succeed Stevens at its last delegate conference, held in Freetown in November 1985. The candidate was <a href="/wiki/Major_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Major General">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Saidu_Momoh" title="Joseph Saidu Momoh">Joseph Saidu Momoh</a>, head of the Sierra Leone Armed Forces and Stevens' own choice to succeed him. As head of the armed forces, General Momoh had been very loyal to Stevens, who had appointed him to the position. Like Stevens, Momoh was also a member of the minority <a href="/wiki/Limba_people_(Sierra_Leone)" title="Limba people (Sierra Leone)">Limba</a> ethnic group. </p>
      <p>As the sole candidate, Momoh was elected president without opposition and sworn in as Sierra Leone's second president on 28 November 1985 in Freetown. A one-party parliamentary election between APC members was held in May 1986. President Momoh appointed his former military colleague and key ally, Major General Mohamed Tarawalie to succeed him as the head of the Sierra Leone Military. General Tarawalie was also a strong loyalist and key Momoh supporter. President Momoh named James Bambay Kamara as the head of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Police" title="Sierra Leone Police">Sierra Leone Police</a>. Bambay Kamara was also a strong Momoh loyalist and supporter. Momoh broke from former President Siaka Stevens by integrating the powerful SSD into the Sierra Leone Police as a special <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramilitary force">paramilitary force</a>. Under President Stevens, the SSD had been a powerful personal force used to maintain his hold on power, independent from the Sierra Leone Military and Sierra Leone Police Force. The Sierra Leone Police under Bambay Kamara's leadership, was accused of physical violence, arrest and intimidation against critics of President Momoh's government. </p>
      <p>President Momoh's strong links with the army and his verbal attacks on corruption earned him much-needed initial support among Sierra Leoneans. With the lack of new faces in the new APC cabinet under president Momoh and the return of many of the old faces from Stevens' government, criticisms soon arose that Momoh was simply perpetuating the rule of Stevens. </p>
      <p>The next few years under the Momoh administration were characterised by corruption, which Momoh defused by sacking several senior cabinet ministers. To formalise his war against corruption, President Momoh announced a "<a href="/wiki/Code_of_Conduct" class="mw-redirect" title="Code of Conduct">Code of Conduct</a> for Political Leaders and Public Servants". After an alleged attempt to overthrow President Momoh in March 1987, more than 60 senior government officials were arrested, including Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Francis_Minah" title="Francis Minah">Francis Minah</a>, who was removed from office, convicted of plotting the coup, and executed by <a href="/wiki/Hanging" title="Hanging">hanging</a> in 1989, along with five others. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Sierra_Leone_Civil_War_.281991.E2.80.932002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sierra_Leone_Civil_War_(1991–2002)">Sierra Leone Civil War (1991–2002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sierra Leone Civil War (1991–2002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg/300px-School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg/450px-School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg/600px-School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1577" data-file-height="1081"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:School_destroyed_by_Sierra_Leone_Civil_War.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A school in <a href="/wiki/Koindu" title="Koindu">Koindu</a> destroyed during the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Civil War</a>; in total 1,270 primary schools were destroyed in the War.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-56">[56]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In October 1990, owing to mounting pressure from both within and outside the country for political and economic reform, president Momoh set up a constitutional review commission to assess the 1978 one-party constitution. Based on the commission's recommendations a constitution re-establishing a multiparty system was approved by the exclusive APC Parliament by a 60% majority vote, becoming effective on 1 October 1991. There was great suspicion that president Momoh was not serious about his promise of political reform, as APC rule continued to be increasingly marked by abuses of power. </p>
      <p>The brutal civil war that was going on in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> played a significant role in the outbreak of fighting in Sierra Leone. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(Liberia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles Taylor (Liberia)">Charles Taylor</a> – then leader of the <a href="/wiki/National_Patriotic_Front_of_Liberia" title="National Patriotic Front of Liberia">National Patriotic Front of Liberia</a> – reportedly helped form the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_United_Front" title="Revolutionary United Front">Revolutionary United Front (RUF)</a> under the command of former Sierra Leonean army <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">corporal</a> <a href="/wiki/Foday_Sankoh" title="Foday Sankoh">Foday Saybana Sankoh</a>, an ethnic Temne from <a href="/wiki/Tonkolili_District" title="Tonkolili District">Tonkolili District</a> in Northern Sierra Leone. Sankoh was a British trained former army corporal who had also undergone guerrilla training in Libya. Taylor's aim was for the RUF to attack the bases of Nigerian dominated peacekeeping troops in Sierra Leone who were opposed to his rebel movement in Liberia. </p>
      <p>On 29 April 1992, a group of young soldiers in the Sierra Leone Army, led by seven army officers — Lieutenant Sahr Sandy, Captain <a href="/wiki/Valentine_Strasser" title="Valentine Strasser">Valentine Strasser</a>, Sergeant <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Musa" title="Solomon Musa">Solomon Musa</a>, Captain <a href="/wiki/Komba_Mondeh" title="Komba Mondeh">Komba Mondeh</a>, Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Tom_Nyuma" title="Tom Nyuma">Tom Nyuma</a>, Captain <a href="/wiki/Julius_Maada_Bio" title="Julius Maada Bio">Julius Maada Bio</a> and Captain Komba Kambo—<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> launched a <a href="/wiki/Military_coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Military coup">military coup</a> that sent president Momoh into <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exile</a> in Guinea, and the young soldiers established the National Provisional Ruling Council (NPRC), with 25-year-old Captain Valentine Strasser as its chairman and Head of State of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-blogspot1_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogspot1-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sergeant Solomon Musa, a childhood friend of Strasser, became the deputy chairman and deputy leader of the NPRC <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">junta</a> government. Strasser became the world's youngest Head of State when he seized power just three days after his 25th birthday. The NPRC junta established the National Supreme Council of State as the military highest command and final authority in all matters, and was exclusively made up of the highest ranking NPRC soldiers, included Strasser himself and the original soldiers who toppled president Momoh.<sup id="cite_ref-blogspot1_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogspot1-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>One of the highest ranking soldiers of the NPRC Junta, Lieutenant Sahr Sandy, a trusted ally of Strasser, was assassinated, allegedly by Major S.I.M. Turay, a key loyalist of ousted president Momoh. A heavily armed military manhunt took place across the country to find Lieutenant Sandy's killer. However, the main suspect, Major S.I.M Turay, went into hiding and fled the country to Guinea, fearing for his life. Dozens of soldiers loyal to the ousted president Momoh were arrested, including Colonel Kahota M. Dumbuya and Major Yayah Turay. Lieutenant Sandy was given a <a href="/wiki/State_funeral" title="State funeral">state funeral</a> and his funeral prayers service at the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral" title="Cathedral">cathedral</a> church in Freetown was attended by many high-ranking soldiers of the NPRC junta, including Strasser himself and NPRC deputy leader Sergeant Solomon Musa. </p>
      <p>The NPRC Junta immediately suspended the constitution, banned all political parties, limited <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a> and enacted a rule-by-decree policy, in which soldiers were granted unlimited powers of administrative detention without charge or trial, and challenges against such detentions in court were precluded. </p>
      <p>The NPRC Junta maintained relations with the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS) and strengthened support for Sierra Leone-based <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States_Monitoring_Group" title="Economic Community of West African States Monitoring Group">ECOMOG</a> troops fighting in Liberia. On 28 December 1992, an alleged coup attempt against the NPRC government of Strasser, aimed at freeing the detained Colonel Yahya Kanu, Colonel Kahota M.S. Dumbuya and former inspector general of police Bambay Kamara, was foiled. Several Junior army officers led by Sergeant Mohamed Lamin Bangura were identified as being behind the coup plot.
