The coup plot led to the <a href="/wiki/Firing_squad" class="mw-redirect" title="Firing squad">firing squad</a> execution of seventeen soldiers in the Sierra Leone Army including Colonel Kahota M Dumbuya, Major Yayah Kanu and Sergeant Mohamed Lamin Bangura. Several prominent members of the Momoh government who had been in detention at the Pa Demba Road prison, including former inspector general of police Bambay Kamara, were also executed.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 5 July 1994 the deputy NPRC leader Sergeant Solomon Musa, who was very popular with the general population, particularly in Freetown, was arrested and sent into exile after he was accused of planning a coup to topple Strasser, an accusation Sergeant Musa denied. Strasser replaced Musa as deputy NPRC chairman with Captain Julius Maada Bio, who was instantly promoted by Strasser to <a href="/wiki/Brigadier" title="Brigadier">Brigadier</a>. </p>
      <p>The NPRC proved to be nearly as ineffectual as the Momoh-led APC government in repelling the RUF. More and more of the country fell to RUF fighters, and by 1994 they held much of the diamond-rich Eastern Province and were at the edge of Freetown. In response, the NPRC hired several hundred mercenaries from the private firm <a href="/wiki/Executive_Outcomes" title="Executive Outcomes">Executive Outcomes</a>. Within a month they had driven RUF fighters back to enclaves along Sierra Leone's borders, and cleared the RUF from the Kono diamond-producing areas of Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p>With Strasser's two most senior NPRC allies and commanders Lieutenant Sahr Sandy and Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Musa" title="Solomon Musa">Solomon Musa</a> no longer around to defend him, Strasser's leadership within the NPRC Supreme Council of State was not considered much stronger. On 16 January 1996, after about four years in power, Strasser was arrested in a palace coup at the Defence Headquarters in Freetown by his fellow NPRC soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-FSL_Vol_2_No_1_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSL_Vol_2_No_1-60">[60]</a></sup> Strasser was immediately flown into exile in a <a href="/wiki/Military_helicopter" title="Military helicopter">military helicopter</a> to <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>. </p>
      <p>In his first public broadcast to the nation following the 1996 coup, Brigadier Bio stated that his support for returning Sierra Leone to a democratically elected civilian government and his commitment to ending the civil war were his motivations for the coup.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Promises of a return to civilian rule were fulfilled by Bio, who handed power over to <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a>, of the Sierra Leone People's Party (SLPP), after the conclusion of elections in early 1996. President Kabbah took power with a great promise of ending the civil war. President Kabbah opened <a href="/wiki/Dialogue" title="Dialogue">dialogue</a> with the RUF and invited RUF leader Foday Sankoh for peace negotiations. </p>
      <p>On 25 May 1997, seventeen soldiers in the Sierra Leone army led by Corporal Tamba Gborie, loyal to the detained <a href="/wiki/Major_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Major General">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Paul_Koroma" title="Johnny Paul Koroma">Johnny Paul Koroma</a>, launched a military coup which sent President Kabbah into exile in Guinea and they established the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_Revolutionary_Council" title="Armed Forces Revolutionary Council">Armed Forces Revolutionary Council</a> (AFRC). Corporal Gborie quickly went to the Sierra Leone Broadcasting Services headquarters in New England, Freetown to announce the coup to a shocked nation and to alert all soldiers across the country to report for guard duty. The soldiers immediately released Koroma from prison and installed him as their chairman and Head of State. </p>
      <p>Koroma suspended the constitution, banned demonstrations, shut down all private radio stations in the country and invited the RUF to join the new junta government, with its leader Foday Sankoh as the Vice-Chairman of the new AFRC-RUF coalition junta government. Within days, Freetown was overwhelmed by the presence of the RUF combatants who came to the city in thousands. The Kamajors, a group of traditional fighters mostly from the Mende ethnic group under the command of deputy <a href="/wiki/Defence_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence Minister">Defence Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Hinga_Norman" title="Samuel Hinga Norman">Samuel Hinga Norman</a>, remained loyal to President Kabbah and defended the Southern part of Sierra Leone from the soldiers. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Kabbah.27s_government_and_the_end_of_civil_war_.282002.E2.80.932014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kabbah's_government_and_the_end_of_civil_war_(2002–2014)">Kabbah's government and the end of civil war (2002–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Kabbah's government and the end of civil war (2002–2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2013</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>After nine months in office, the junta was overthrown by the Nigerian-led <a href="/wiki/ECOMOG" class="mw-redirect" title="ECOMOG">ECOMOG</a> forces, and the democratically elected government of president Kabbah was reinstated in February 1998. On 19 October 1998 24 soldiers in the Sierra Leone army were executed by firing squad after they were convicted in a <a href="/wiki/Court_martial" class="mw-redirect" title="Court martial">court martial</a> in Freetown, some for orchestrating the 1997 coup that overthrew President Kabbah and others for failure to reverse the mutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 1999, the United Nations agreed to send <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeepers</a> to help restore order and disarm the rebels. The first of the 6,000-member force began arriving in December, and the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a> voted in February 2000 to increase the force to 11,000, and later to 13,000. But in May, when nearly all <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigerian</a> forces had left and UN forces were trying to disarm the RUF in eastern Sierra Leone, <a href="/wiki/Foday_Sankoh" title="Foday Sankoh">Sankoh</a>'s forces clashed with the UN troops, and some 500 peacekeepers were taken <a href="/wiki/Hostage" title="Hostage">hostage</a> as the peace accord effectively collapsed. The hostage crisis resulted in more fighting between the RUF and the government as UN troops launched <a href="/wiki/Operation_Khukri" title="Operation Khukri">Operation Khukri</a> to end the siege. The Operation was successful with Indian and British <a href="/wiki/Special_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Forces">Special Forces</a> being the main contingents. </p>
      <p>The situation in the country deteriorated to such an extent that British troops were deployed in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Palliser" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Palliser">Operation Palliser</a>, originally simply to evacuate foreign nationals. However, the British exceeded their original mandate, and took full military action to finally defeat the rebels and restore order. The British were the catalyst for the ceasefire that ended the civil war. Elements of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, together with administrators and politicians, remain in Sierra Leone to this day,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> helping train the armed forces, improve the infrastructure of the country and administer financial and material aid. <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>, the Prime Minister of Britain at the time of the British intervention, is regarded as a hero by the people of Sierra Leone, many of whom are keen for more British involvement.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Sierra Leoneans have been described<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (October 2019)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> as "The World's Most Resilient People".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 1991 and 2001, about <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">50,000 people were killed</a> in Sierra Leone's civil war. Hundreds of thousands of people were forced from their homes and many became refugees in <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>. In 2001, UN forces moved into rebel-held areas and began to disarm rebel soldiers. By January 2002, the war was declared over. In May 2002, <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Kabbah</a> was re-elected president by a landslide. By 2004, the disarmament process was complete. Also in 2004, a UN-backed <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> court began holding trials of senior leaders from both sides of the war. In December 2005, UN peacekeeping forces pulled out of Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p>In August 2007, Sierra Leone held presidential and parliamentary elections. However, no presidential candidate won the 50% plus one vote majority stipulated in the constitution on the first round of voting. A runoff election was held in September 2007, and <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bai_Koroma" title="Ernest Bai Koroma">Ernest Bai Koroma</a>, the candidate of the main opposition APC, was elected president. Koroma was re-elected president for a second (and final) term in November 2012. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Struggle_with_the_Ebola_epidemic_.282014.E2.80.932016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_with_the_Ebola_epidemic_(2014–2016)">Struggle with the Ebola epidemic (2014–2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Struggle with the Ebola epidemic (2014–2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2014 an <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Sierra Leone">Ebola virus epidemic in Sierra Leone</a> began, which had widespread impact on the country,<sup id="cite_ref-internationalsos.com_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internationalsos.com-64">[64]</a></sup> including forcing Sierra Leone to declare a state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> By the end of 2014 there were nearly 3000 deaths and about 10 thousand cases of the disease in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-internationalsos.com_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-internationalsos.com-64">[64]</a></sup> The epidemic also led to the <a href="/wiki/Ouse_to_Ouse_Tock" title="Ouse to Ouse Tock">Ouse to Ouse Tock</a> in September 2014, a nationwide three-day quarantine.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The epidemic occurred as part of the wider <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a>. In early August 2014 Sierra Leone cancelled league football (soccer) matches because of the Ebola epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> On 16 March 2016, the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organisation</a> declared Sierra Leone to be free from Ebola.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="14_August_2017_mudslides">14 August 2017 mudslides</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 14 August 2017 mudslides">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2017_Sierra_Leone_mudslides" title="2017 Sierra Leone mudslides">2017 Sierra Leone mudslides</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Several mudslides occurred around 6:30 AM on the fourteenth of August 2017 in and near the country's capital <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_general_election">2018 general election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2018 general election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2018, Sierra Leone held a <a href="/wiki/2018_Sierra_Leonean_general_election" title="2018 Sierra Leonean general election">general election</a>. The presidential election, in which neither candidate reached the required threshold of 55%, went to a second round of voting, in which Julius Maada Bio was elected with 51% of the vote. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Geography of Sierra Leone">Geography of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UNsierraleone.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/UNsierraleone.PNG/330px-UNsierraleone.PNG" decoding="async" width="330" height="414" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/UNsierraleone.PNG/495px-UNsierraleone.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/UNsierraleone.PNG/660px-UNsierraleone.PNG 2x" data-file-width="2349" data-file-height="2947"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UNsierraleone.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Sierra Leone
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1174" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SLE_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sierra Leone map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sierra Leone is located on the southwest coast of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, lying mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/7th_parallel_north" title="7th parallel north">7°</a> and <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_north" title="10th parallel north">10°N</a> (a small area is south of 7°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/10th_meridian_west" title="10th meridian west">10°</a> and <a href="/wiki/14th_meridian_west" title="14th meridian west">14°W</a>. The country is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> to the north and east, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> to the southeast, and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west and southwest.<sup id="cite_ref-LeVertP7_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeVertP7-69">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone has a total area of 71,740&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (27,699&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), divided into a land area of 71,620&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (27,653&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and water of 120&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (46&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup> The country has four distinct geographical regions. In eastern Sierra Leone the <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateau</a> is interspersed with high mountains, where <a href="/wiki/Mount_Bintumani" title="Mount Bintumani">Mount Bintumani</a> reaches 1,948&nbsp;m (6,391&nbsp;ft), the highest point in the country. The upper part of the <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basin</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Moa_River" title="Moa River">Moa River</a> is located in the south of this region. </p>
      <p>The centre of the country is a region of <a href="/wiki/Lowland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowland">lowland</a> <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a>, containing forests, <a href="/wiki/The_bush" title="The bush">bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">farmland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-LeVertP7_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeVertP7-69">[69]</a></sup> that occupies about 43% of Sierra Leone's land area. The northern section of this has been categorised by the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>, while the south is rain-forested plains and farmland. </p>
      <p>In the west, Sierra Leone has some 400&nbsp;km (249&nbsp;mi) of Atlantic coastline, giving it both bountiful marine resources and attractive tourist potential. The coast has areas of low-lying <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a> swamp. The national capital <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a> sits on a coastal <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a>, situated next to the Sierra Leone Harbour. </p>
      <p>The climate is tropical, with two seasons determining the agricultural cycle: the <a href="/wiki/Rainy_season" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainy season">rainy season</a> from May to November, and a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> from December to May, which includes <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">harmattan</a>, when cool, dry winds blow in off the <a href="/wiki/Sahara_Desert" class="mw-redirect" title="Sahara Desert">Sahara Desert</a> and the night-time temperature can be as low as 16&nbsp;°C (60.8&nbsp;°F). The average temperature is 26&nbsp;°C (78.8&nbsp;°F) and varies from around 26 to 36&nbsp;°C (78.8 to 96.8&nbsp;°F) during the year.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Wildlife of Sierra Leone">Wildlife of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Sierra Leone is home to four terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Guinean_montane_forests" title="Guinean montane forests">Guinean montane forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Guinean_lowland_forests" title="Western Guinean lowland forests">Western Guinean lowland forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinean_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Guinean forest-savanna mosaic">Guinean forest-savanna mosaic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinean_mangroves" title="Guinean mangroves">Guinean mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Human activities claimed to be responsible or contributing to <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">land degradation</a> in Sierra Leone include unsustainable agricultural land use, poor soil and water management practices, deforestation, removal of natural vegetation, fuelwood consumption and to a lesser extent overgrazing and urbanisation.<sup id="cite_ref-unccd_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unccd-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">Deforestation</a>, both for commercial timber and to make room for agriculture, is the major concern and represents an enormous loss of natural economic wealth to the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-unccd_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unccd-74">[74]</a></sup> Mining and <a href="/wiki/Slash_and_burn" class="mw-redirect" title="Slash and burn">slash and burn</a> for land conversion – such as cattle grazing – dramatically diminished forested land in Sierra Leone since the 1980s. It is listed among countries of concern for emissions, as having Low Forest Cover with High Rates of Deforestation (LFHD).<sup id="cite_ref-Angelsen,_Arild_et_al_2009_75–77_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angelsen,_Arild_et_al_2009_75–77-75">[75]</a></sup> There are concerns that heavy logging continues in the Tama-Tonkoli Forest Reserve in the north. Loggers have extended their operations to Nimini, Kono District, Eastern Province; Jui, Western Rural District, Western Area; Loma Mountains National Park, Koinadougu, Northern Province; and with plans to start operations in the Kambui Forest reserve in the Kenema District, Eastern Province.<sup id="cite_ref-Angelsen,_Arild_et_al_2009_75–77_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angelsen,_Arild_et_al_2009_75–77-75">[75]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 2.76/10, ranking it 154th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-76">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/West_Africa#Overfishing" title="West Africa">Overfishing</a> is also an issue in Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">Habitat</a> degradation for the <a href="/wiki/African_wild_dog" title="African wild dog">African wild dog</a>, <i>Lycaon pictus</i>, has been increased, such that this <a href="/wiki/Canidae" title="Canidae">canid</a> is deemed to have been extirpated in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until 2002, Sierra Leone lacked a forest management system because of the civil war that caused tens of thousands of deaths. Deforestation rates have increased 7.3% since the end of the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.mongabay.com_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.mongabay.com-78">[78]</a></sup> On paper, 55 protected areas covered 4.5% of Sierra Leone as of 2003. The country has 2,090 known <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of higher plants, 147 <a href="/wiki/Mammals" class="mw-redirect" title="Mammals">mammals</a>, 626 birds, 67 <a href="/wiki/Reptiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Reptiles">reptiles</a>, 35 <a href="/wiki/Amphibians" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphibians">amphibians</a>, and 99 fish species.<sup id="cite_ref-rainforests.mongabay.com_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainforests.mongabay.com-78">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Justice_Foundation" title="Environmental Justice Foundation">Environmental Justice Foundation</a> has documented how the number of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_fishing" class="mw-redirect" title="Illegal fishing">illegal fishing</a> vessels in Sierra Leone's waters has multiplied in recent years. The amount of illegal fishing has significantly depleted fish stocks, depriving local fishing communities of an important resource for survival. The situation is particularly serious as fishing provides the only source of income for many communities in a country still recovering from over a decade of civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">Royal Society for the Protection of Birds</a> (RSPB) and BirdLife International agreed to support a conservation-<a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> project in the <a href="/wiki/Gola_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Gola Forest">Gola Forest</a> in south eastern Sierra Leone,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> an important surviving fragment of <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> in Sierra Leone. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Politics of Sierra Leone">Politics of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg/220px-Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg/330px-Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg/440px-Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="1170"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ernest_Bai_Koroma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bai_Koroma" title="Ernest Bai Koroma">Ernest Bai Koroma</a>, former president of Sierra Leone
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sierra Leone is a constitutional republic with a <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">directly elected</a> president and a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral_legislature" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral legislature">unicameral legislature</a>. The current system of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Government of Sierra Leone">Government of Sierra Leone</a> is based on the 1991 Sierra Leone Constitution. Sierra Leone has a dominant <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Central_government" title="Central government">central government</a> and a weak <a href="/wiki/Local_government" title="Local government">local government</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> of the Government of Sierra Leone, headed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sierra_Leone" title="President of Sierra Leone">president of Sierra Leone</a> has extensive powers and influences. The president is the most powerful government official in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-nyulawglobal.org_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyulawglobal.org-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Within the confines of the 1991 Constitution, supreme legislative powers are vested in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Parliament of Sierra Leone">Parliament</a>, which is the law making body of the nation. Supreme executive authority rests in the president and members of his cabinet and judicial power with the judiciary of which the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Justice of Sierra Leone">Chief Justice of Sierra Leone</a> is the head. </p>
      <p>The president is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone Armed Forces</a>. The president appoints and heads a cabinet of ministers, which must be approved by the Parliament. The president is elected by <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">popular vote</a> to a maximum of two five-year terms. The president is the highest and most influential position within the government of Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p>To be elected president of Sierra Leone, a candidate must gain at least 55% of the vote. If no candidate gets 55%, there is a <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">second-round runoff</a> between the top two candidates. </p>
      <p>The current president of Sierra Leone is former <a href="/wiki/Military_junta" title="Military junta">military junta</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Julius_Maada_Bio" title="Julius Maada Bio">Julius Maada Bio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-82">[82]</a></sup> Bio defeated <a href="/wiki/Samura_Kamara" title="Samura Kamara">Samura Kamara</a> of the ruling <a href="/wiki/All_People%27s_Congress" title="All People's Congress">All People's Congress</a> in the country's tightly contested 2018 presidential election. Bio replaced outgoing President <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Bai_Koroma" title="Ernest Bai Koroma">Ernest Bai Koroma</a> after Bio was sworn into office on 4 April 2018 by Chief Justice <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abdulai_Cham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abdulai Cham (page does not exist)">Abdulai Cham</a>. Bio is the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">Sierra Leone People's Party</a>, the current ruling party in Sierra Leone. </p>
      <p>Next to the president is the <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice President of Sierra Leone">Vice-president</a>, who is the second-highest ranking government official in the executive branch of the Sierra Leone Government. As designated by the Sierra Leone Constitution, the vice-president is to become the new president of Sierra Leone upon the death, resignation, or removal of the President. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Freetown_Court_1984.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Freetown_Court_1984.jpg/250px-Freetown_Court_1984.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Freetown_Court_1984.jpg/375px-Freetown_Court_1984.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Freetown_Court_1984.jpg/500px-Freetown_Court_1984.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="1344"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Freetown_Court_1984.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Sierra Leone <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Supreme Court of Sierra Leone">Supreme Court</a> in the capital <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, the highest and most powerful court in the country
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Parliament of Sierra Leone">Parliament of Sierra Leone</a> is <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a>, with 124 seats. Each of the country's fourteen districts is represented in parliament. 112 members are elected concurrently with the presidential elections; the other 12 seats are filled by <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chief" title="Paramount chief">paramount chiefs</a> from each of the country's 12 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Districts of Sierra Leone">administrative districts</a>. The Sierra Leone parliament is led by the Speaker of Parliament, who is the overall leader of Parliament and is directly elected by sitting members of parliament. The current speaker of the Sierra Leone parliament is <a href="/wiki/Sheku_Badara_Bashiru_Dumbuya" title="Sheku Badara Bashiru Dumbuya">Sheku Badara Bashiru Dumbuya</a>, who was elected by members of parliament on 21 January 2014. </p>
      <p>The current members of Parliament of Sierra Leone were elected in the 2012 Sierra Leone parliamentary election. The <a href="/wiki/All_People%27s_Congress" title="All People's Congress">All People's Congress</a> (APC) currently has 70 of the 112 elected parliamentary seats and the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_People%27s_Party" title="Sierra Leone People's Party">Sierra Leone People's Party</a> (SLPP) has 42 of the elected 132 parliamentary seats. Sierra Leone's two most dominant <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">parties</a>, the APC and the SLPP, collectively won every elected seats in Parliament in the 2012 Sierra Leone parliamentary election. To be qualified as Member of Parliament, the person must be a citizen of Sierra Leone, must be at least 21 years old, must be able to speak, read and write the English language with a degree of proficiency to enable him to actively take part in proceedings in Parliament; and must not have any criminal conviction.<sup id="cite_ref-nyulawglobal.org_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyulawglobal.org-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since independence in 1961, Sierra Leone's politics has been dominated by two major political parties: the SLPP and the APC. Other minor political parties have also existed but with no significant support.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Judiciary of Sierra Leone">Judiciary of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The judicial power of Sierra Leone is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a>, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Justice of Sierra Leone">Chief Justice of Sierra Leone</a> and comprising the Supreme Court of Sierra Leone, which is the highest court in the country, meaning that its rulings therefore cannot be appealed against. Other courts include the High Court of Justice, the Court of Appeal, the magistrate courts, and traditional courts in rural villages. The president appoints and parliament approves Justices for the three courts. The Judiciary have jurisdiction in all civil and criminal matters throughout the country. The current acting <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Justice">Chief Justice</a> of Sierra Leone is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Valicious_Thomas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Valicious Thomas (page does not exist)">Valicious Thomas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Foreign relations of Sierra Leone">Foreign relations of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG/220px-Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG/330px-Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG/440px-Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1871" data-file-height="2028"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Sierra_Leone.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Embassy of Sierra Leone in Washington, D.C.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Sierra Leonean Ministry of Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation is responsible for foreign policy of Sierra Leone. Sierra Leone has diplomatic relations that include China, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone has good relations with the West, including the United States, and has maintained historical ties with the United Kingdom and other former <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British colonies</a> through its membership of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The United Kingdom has played a major role in providing aid to the former colony, together with administrative help and military training since intervening to end the Civil War in 2000. </p>
      <p>Former President <a href="/wiki/Siaka_Stevens" title="Siaka Stevens">Siaka Stevens</a>' government had sought closer relations with other <a href="/wiki/West_African" class="mw-redirect" title="West African">West African</a> countries under the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS) a policy continued by the current government. Sierra Leone, along with <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, form the <a href="/wiki/Mano_River_Union" title="Mano River Union">Mano River Union</a> (MRU). It is primarily designed to implement development projects and promote regional <a href="/wiki/Economic_integration" title="Economic integration">economic integration</a> between the three countries.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone is also a member of the United Nations and its specialised agencies, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a> (AFDB), the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC), and the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (NAM).<sup id="cite_ref-foreign_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreign-88">[88]</a></sup> Sierra Leone is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_Immunity_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral Immunity Agreement">Bilateral Immunity Agreement</a> of protection for the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of the United States">US military</a> (as covered under Article 98). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Sierra Leone">Administrative divisions of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg/350px-Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="350" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg/525px-Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg/700px-Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1606" data-file-height="1606"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Districts_in_Sierra_Leone_2018.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 14 districts and 2 areas of Sierra Leone
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of Sierra Leone is composed of four regions: the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Province,_Sierra_Leone" title="Northern Province, Sierra Leone">Northern Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Province,_Sierra_Leone" title="Southern Province, Sierra Leone">Southern Province</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Sierra_Leone" title="Eastern Province, Sierra Leone">Eastern Province</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Area" title="Western Area">Western Area</a>. Three provinces are further divided into 12 districts; and the Western Area is divided into two districts. </p>
      <p>The provincial districts are divided into 149 chiefdoms, which have traditionally been led by <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chiefs" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramount chiefs">paramount chiefs</a>, recognised by the British administration in 1896 at the time of organising the Protectorate of Sierra Leone. The Paramount Chiefs are very influential, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Villages" class="mw-redirect" title="Villages">villages</a> and small rural towns.<sup id="cite_ref-tristan_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tristan-89">[89]</a></sup> Each chiefdom has ruling families that were recognised at that time; the Tribal Authority, made up of local notables, elects the paramount chief from the ruling families.<sup id="cite_ref-tristan_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tristan-89">[89]</a></sup> Typically, chiefs have the power to "raise taxes, control the judicial system, and allocate land, the most important resource in rural areas."<sup id="cite_ref-daron_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daron-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Within the context of local governance, the districts are governed as <i>localities</i>. Each has a directly elected local district council to exercise authority and carry out functions at a local level.<sup id="cite_ref-Renner-Thomas_2010_6–7_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-Thomas_2010_6–7-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> In total, there are 19 local councils: 13 district councils, one for each of the 12 districts and one for the Western Area Rural, and six municipalities also have elected local councils. The six municipalities include <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, which functions as the local government for the Western Area Urban District, and <a href="/wiki/Bo,_Sierra_Leone" title="Bo, Sierra Leone">Bo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonthe" title="Bonthe">Bonthe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenema" title="Kenema">Kenema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koidu" title="Koidu">Koidu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Makeni" title="Makeni">Makeni</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Renner-Thomas_2010_6–7_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-Thomas_2010_6–7-91">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While the district councils are under the oversight of their respective provincial administrations, the municipalities are directly overseen by the Ministry of Local Government &amp; Community Development and thus administratively independent of district and provincial administrations. </p>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Sierra Leone">Military of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Military of Sierra Leone, officially the Republic of Sierra Leone Armed Forces (RSLAF), are the unified armed forces of Sierra Leone responsible for the territorial security of Sierra Leone's border and defending the national interests of Sierra Leone within the framework of its international obligations. The armed forces were formed after independence in 1961, on the basis of elements of the former British <a href="/wiki/Royal_West_African_Frontier_Force" title="Royal West African Frontier Force">Royal West African Frontier Force</a> present in the country. The Sierra Leone Armed Forces consists of around 15,500 personnel, comprising the largest Sierra Leone Army,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> the Sierra Leone Navy and the Sierra Leone Air Wing.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sierra_Leone" title="President of Sierra Leone">President of Sierra Leone</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Commander_in_Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander in Chief">Commander in Chief</a> of the military, with the Minister of Defence responsible for defence policy and the formulation of the armed forces. The current Sierra Leonean Defence Minister is retired Major <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Conteh" class="mw-redirect" title="Paolo Conteh">Alfred Paolo Conteh</a>. The Military of Sierra Leone also has a <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Staff_(Sierra_Leone)" title="Chief of the Defence Staff (Sierra Leone)">Chief of the Defence Staff</a> who is a uniformed <a href="/wiki/Military_official" class="mw-redirect" title="Military official">military official</a> responsible for the administration and the operational control of the Sierra Leone military.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brigadier_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Brigadier General">Brigadier General</a> <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nelson-Williams" title="Alfred Nelson-Williams">Alfred Nelson-Williams</a> who was appointed by president Koroma succeeded the retired <a href="/wiki/Major_General" class="mw-redirect" title="Major General">Major General</a> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Sam_M%27boma" title="Edward Sam M'boma">Edward Sam M'boma</a> on 12 September 2008 as the Chief of Defence Staff of the Military.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When Sierra Leone gained independence in 1961, the Royal Sierra Leone Military Force was created from the Sierra Leone Battalion of the West African Frontier Force.<sup id="cite_ref-Kaplan_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan-109">[109]</a></sup> The military seized control in 1968, bringing the <a href="/wiki/National_Reformation_Council" title="National Reformation Council">National Reformation Council</a> into power. On 19 April 1971, when Sierra Leone became a republic, the Royal Sierra Leone Military Forces were renamed the Republic of Sierra Leone Military Force (RSLMF).<sup id="cite_ref-Kaplan_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaplan-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> The RSLMF remained a single-service organisation until 1979, when the Sierra Leone Navy was established. In 1995 Defence Headquarters was established, and the Sierra Leone Air Wing formed. The RSLMF was renamed as the Armed Forces of the Republic of Sierra Leone (AFRSL). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Law enforcement in Sierra Leone is primarily the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Police" title="Sierra Leone Police">Sierra Leone Police</a> (SLP), which is accountable to the Minister of Internal Affairs (appointed by the president). Sierra Leone Police was established by the <a href="/wiki/British_colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British colony">British colony</a> in 1894; it is one of the oldest police forces in West Africa. It works to prevent crime, protect life and property, detect and prosecute offenders, maintain <a href="/wiki/Public_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Public order">public order</a>, ensure safety and security, and enhance access to justice. The Sierra Leone Police is headed by the <a href="/wiki/Inspector_General_of_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Inspector General of Police">Inspector General of Police</a>, the professional head of the Sierra Leone Police force, who is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sierra_Leone" title="President of Sierra Leone">President of Sierra Leone</a>. </p>
      <p>Each one of <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Districts of Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone's 14 districts</a> is headed by a district police commissioner who is the professional head of their respective district. These Police Commissioners report directly to the Inspector General of Police at the Sierra Leone Police headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>. The current Inspector General of Police is <a href="/wiki/Brima_Acha_Kamara" title="Brima Acha Kamara">Brima Acha Kamara</a>, who was appointed to the position by former president <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Human rights in Sierra Leone">Human rights in Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Sierra_Leone" title="LGBT rights in Sierra Leone">same-sex sexual activity</a> is illegal under Section 61 of the <a href="/wiki/Offences_against_the_Person_Act_1861" class="mw-redirect" title="Offences against the Person Act 1861">Offences against the Person Act 1861</a>, and imprisonment for life is possible.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Economy of Sierra Leone">Economy of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png/350px-Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png/525px-Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png/700px-Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="855" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Leone_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Sierra Leone's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By the 1990s economic activity was declining and economic infrastructure had become seriously degraded. Over the next decade much of the formal economy was destroyed in the country's civil war. Since the end of hostilities in January 2002, massive infusions of outside assistance have helped Sierra Leone begin to recover.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Much of the recovery will depend on the success of the government's efforts to limit corruption by officials, which many feel was the chief cause for the civil war. A key indicator of success will be the effectiveness of government management of its diamond sector. </p>
      <p>There is high unemployment, particularly among the youth and ex-combatants. Authorities have been slow to implement reforms in the civil service, and the pace of the privatisation programme is also slackening and donors have urged its advancement. </p>
      <p>The currency is the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_leone" title="Sierra Leonean leone">leone</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Bank of Sierra Leone">Bank of Sierra Leone</a>. Sierra Leone operates a floating <a href="/wiki/Exchange_rate" title="Exchange rate">exchange rate</a> system, and foreign currencies can be exchanged at any of the commercial banks, recognised foreign exchange <a href="/wiki/Service_bureau" title="Service bureau">bureaux</a> and most hotels. Credit card use is limited in Sierra Leone, though they may be used at some hotels and restaurants. There are a few internationally linked <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">automated teller machines</a> that accept <a href="/wiki/Visa_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa card">Visa cards</a> in Freetown operated by ProCredit Bank. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Agriculture in Sierra Leone">Agriculture in Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg/220px-Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg/330px-Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg/440px-Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1244" data-file-height="816"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra_Leone_rice_farmer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A farmer with his rice harvest in Sierra Leone. Two-thirds of Sierra Leone's population are directly involved in <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-future_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-future-114">[114]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Two-thirds of the population of Sierra Leone are directly involved in <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-future_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-future-114">[114]</a></sup> Agriculture accounted for 58 per cent of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-AFEC_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFEC-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agriculture is the largest employer with 80 per cent of the population working in the sector.<sup id="cite_ref-tour_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tour-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">Rice</a> is the most important staple crop in Sierra Leone with 85 per cent of farmers cultivating rice during the rainy season<sup id="cite_ref-deep_rice_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deep_rice-117">[117]</a></sup> and an annual consumption of 76&nbsp;kg per person.<sup id="cite_ref-rice_facts_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rice_facts-118">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Mining in Sierra Leone">Mining in Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Rich in minerals, Sierra Leone has relied on mining, especially diamonds, for its economic base. The country is among the top ten diamond producing nations. Mineral exports remain the main <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> earner. Sierra Leone is a major producer of gem-quality diamonds. Though rich in diamonds, it has historically struggled to manage their exploitation and export. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone is known for its <a href="/wiki/Blood_diamond" title="Blood diamond">blood diamonds</a> that were mined and sold to diamond conglomerates during the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">civil war</a>, to buy the weapons that fuelled its atrocities.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In the 1970s and early 1980s, economic growth rate slowed because of a decline in the mining sector and increasing corruption among government officials. </p> 
      <table class="wikitable infobox" style="margin-right: 0; margin-left: 1em; text-align:right;"> 
       <caption style="font-size: 115%;">
        Percentage of GDP by sector (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-AFEC_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFEC-115">[115]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col">Rank </th>

         <th scope="col">Percentage<br> of GDP </th>
        </tr>

         <th scope="row">1 </th> 
         <td>Agriculture </td> 
         <td>58.5 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row">2 </th> 
         <td>Other services </td> 
         <td>10.4 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row">3 </th> 
         <td>Trade and tourism </td> 
         <td>9.5 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row">4 </th>

         <td>9.0 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row">5 </th>

         <td>4.5 </td>
        </tr>

        </tr>
