         <td>0.4 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Annual production of Sierra Leone's diamond estimates range between US$250 million–$300&nbsp;million. Some of that is <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggled</a>, where it is possibly used for <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> or financing illicit activities. Formal exports have dramatically improved since the civil war, with efforts to improve the management of them having some success. In October 2000, a UN-approved certification system for exporting diamonds from the country was put in place and led to a dramatic increase in legal exports. In 2001, the government created a mining community development fund (<a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Mineral_Resources_(Sierra_Leone)" title="Ministry of Mineral Resources (Sierra Leone)">DACDF</a>), which returns a portion of diamond export taxes to diamond mining communities. The fund was created to raise local communities' stake in the legal diamond trade. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone has one of the world's largest deposits of <a href="/wiki/Rutile" title="Rutile">rutile</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">titanium</a> ore used as <a href="/wiki/Paint" title="Paint">paint</a> pigment and <a href="/wiki/Welding" title="Welding">welding</a> rod coatings. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_infrastructure">Transport infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Transport infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Transport in Sierra Leone">Transport in Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg/220px-Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg/330px-Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg/440px-Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="814"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kenema-Kailahun_Road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The road from <a href="/wiki/Kenema" title="Kenema">Kenema</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kailahun_District" title="Kailahun District">Kailahun District</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are a number of systems of transport in Sierra Leone, which has a road, air and water infrastructure, including a network of highways and several airports. There are 11,300 kilometres (7,000 miles) of highways in Sierra Leone, of which 904&nbsp;km (562&nbsp;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup> are paved (about 8% of the roads). Sierra Leone's highways are linked to <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a>, Guinea, and <a href="/wiki/Monrovia" title="Monrovia">Monrovia</a>, Liberia. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone has the largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural harbour">natural harbour</a> on the African continent, allowing international shipping through the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II_Quay" title="Queen Elizabeth II Quay">Queen Elizabeth II Quay</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cline_Town,_Sierra_Leone" class="mw-redirect" title="Cline Town, Sierra Leone">Cline Town</a> area of eastern Freetown or through Government Wharf in central Freetown. There are 800&nbsp;km (497&nbsp;mi) of waterways in Sierra Leone, of which 600&nbsp;km (373&nbsp;mi) are navigable year-round. Major port cities are <a href="/wiki/Bonthe" title="Bonthe">Bonthe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherbro_Island" title="Sherbro Island">Sherbro Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepel" title="Pepel">Pepel</a>. </p>
      <p>There are ten <a href="/wiki/Regional_airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional airport">regional airports</a> in Sierra Leone, and one <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lungi_International_Airport" title="Lungi International Airport">Lungi International Airport</a> located in the coastal town of <a href="/wiki/Lungi,_Sierra_Leone" title="Lungi, Sierra Leone">Lungi</a> in Northern Sierra Leone is the primary airport for domestic and international travel to or from Sierra Leone. Passengers cross the river to Aberdeen <a href="/wiki/Heliport" title="Heliport">Heliports</a> in Freetown by <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">hovercraft</a>, ferry or a <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a>. Helicopters are also available from the airport to other major cities in the country. The airport has <a href="/wiki/Pavement_(material)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pavement (material)">paved</a> runways longer than 3,047 metres (9,997 feet). The other airports have unpaved runways, and seven have runways from 914 to 1,523 metres (2,999 to 4,997 feet) long; the remaining two have shorter runways. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone appears on the EU list of prohibited countries with regard to the certification of airlines. This means that no airline registered in Sierra Leone may operate services of any kind within the European Union. This is due to substandard safety standards.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of May 2014 the country's only <a href="/wiki/Lungi_International_Airport" title="Lungi International Airport">international airport</a> had regularly scheduled direct flights to London, Paris, Brussels and most major cities in West Africa. </p>
      <p>In September 2014 there were many Districts with travel restrictions including Kailahun, Kenema, Bombali, Tonkolili, and Port Loko because of <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Ebola virus epidemic in Sierra Leone">Ebola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_in_Sierra_Leone">Energy in Sierra Leone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Energy in Sierra Leone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>As of 2016, about 12% of the population of Sierra Leone had access to electricity. Of the 12%, 10% was in the capital Freetown, and the remaining 90% of the country used 2% of the nation's electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-122">[122]</a></sup> The majority of the population relies on biomass fuels for their daily survival, with firewood and coal used most prevalently.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-123">[123]</a></sup> The burning of these sources has been reported to have adverse health effects on women and children.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-123">[123]</a></sup> A 2012 study was done on the correlation between Acute Respiratory Infection (ARI), and burning biomass fuels in the home. The results were that 64% of children were diagnosed with ARI where firewood stoves were used, and 44% where charcoal stoves were used.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-123">[123]</a></sup> The use of coal and firewood has also posed environmental concerns as they are both conflict with the push for more sustainable sources energy.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-124">[124]</a></sup> As a result, the commercialisation of firewood and coal has been a point of contention with aid donors and government agencies such as the Ministry of Energy and Water Resources and the Forestry Division.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-124">[124]</a></sup> There have been strong pushes for both solar and hydropower to become the dominant sources of energy in Sierra Leone because of the UN's <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>, particularly goal number seven (affordable and clean energy). Sierra Leone's tropical climate, heavy annual rainfall, and abundance of rivers give it potential to realistically pursue more solar and hydropower alternatives.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-125">[125]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_energy">Solar energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Solar energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In conjunction with the UK's <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a> (DFID), Sierra Leone has set the goal to provide solar power to all of its citizens by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[126]</a></sup> This overarching goal has been broken down into smaller goals as well. The first of these goals is to provide solar power to at least 50,000 homes in 2016, the second is 250,000 homes by 2017, and finally to provide power to 1,000,000 people by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[126]</a></sup> This initiative falls under the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Energy_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Energy Africa (page does not exist)">Energy Africa</a> access campaign which seeks to provide electricity to 14 different African countries by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-122">[122]</a></sup> Previous to this compact agreement, Sierra Leone's private sector for solar energy was weak, as it provided energy to less than 5% of the target population.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-122">[122]</a></sup> Part of the reason for this was due to the import duties and taxes and the lack of quality control.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-122">[122]</a></sup> In order to ensure that the Energy Africa goal is met, Sierra Leone has agreed to remove its import duties and Value Added Tax (VAT) on certified solar products.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-126">[126]</a></sup> This change will attempt to encourage foreign investment while providing affordable, quality solar products to its citizens. It is estimated that there will be a 30% to 40% cost reduction on solar products with the lack of duties and taxes.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_122-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-122">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydroelectric_power">Hydroelectric power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Hydroelectric power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>As of 2012, Sierra Leone has 3 main hydroelectric plants. The first is the Guma plant which was decommissioned in 1982, the second is the Dodo Plant which is located in the Eastern Province, and finally the <a href="/wiki/Bumbuna_Dam" title="Bumbuna Dam">Bumbuna plant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-125">[125]</a></sup> There is also potential for several new hydroelectric plants to be opened on the Sewa River, Pampana River, Seli River, Moa River, and Little Scarcies.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-125">[125]</a></sup> Amongst all these projects, both finished and potential, the Bumbuna dam still remains the largest of the hydroelectric projects in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-125">[125]</a></sup> It is located near the Seli River and Freetown and was estimated to produce about 50 megawatts of electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-127">[127]</a></sup> There were plans to increase its capacity 400 megawatts by 2017 which would cost around $750 million.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> It has been projected that the Bumbuna dam could potentially reduce the amount of spending on foreign fuel and save the country at least $2 million a month.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In the past this project received its funding of over $200 million from a combination of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>, and the Italian company <a href="/wiki/Salini_Impregilo" class="mw-redirect" title="Salini Impregilo">Salini Impregilo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-127">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Demographics of Sierra Leone">Demographics of Sierra Leone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Languages of Sierra Leone">Languages of Sierra Leone</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra-Leone-demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sierra-Leone-demography.png/220px-Sierra-Leone-demography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sierra-Leone-demography.png/330px-Sierra-Leone-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Sierra-Leone-demography.png/440px-Sierra-Leone-demography.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sierra-Leone-demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sierra Leone's total population, from 1961 to 2003
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2013 Sierra Leone had an officially projected population of 6,190,280<sup id="cite_ref-Stat.sl_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stat.sl-130">[130]</a></sup> and a growth rate of 2.216% a year.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup> The country's population is mostly young, with an estimated 41.7% under 15, and rural, with an estimated 62% of people living outside the cities.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup> As a result of migration to cities, the population is becoming more urban with an estimated rate of urbanisation growth of 2.9% a year.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Renner-Thomas_2010_5_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-Thomas_2010_5-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Population density varies greatly within Sierra Leone. The <a href="/wiki/Western_Area_Urban_District" title="Western Area Urban District">Western Area Urban District</a>, including Freetown, the capital and largest city, has a population density of 1,224 persons per square km. The largest district geographically, <a href="/wiki/Koinadugu_District" title="Koinadugu District">Koinadugu</a>, has a much lower density of 21.4 persons per square km.<sup id="cite_ref-Renner-Thomas_2010_5_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Renner-Thomas_2010_5-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>English is the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Sierra_Leone_Overview_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sierra_Leone_Overview-132">[132]</a></sup> spoken at schools, government administration and in the media. <a href="/wiki/Krio_language" title="Krio language">Krio</a> (derived from English and several indigenous African languages, and the language of the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Krio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leone Krio people">Sierra Leone Krio people</a>) is the most widely spoken language in virtually all parts of Sierra Leone. As the Krio language is spoken by 90% of the country's population,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_70-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> it unites all the different <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a>, especially in their trade and interaction with each other.<sup id="cite_ref-https://eprints.soas.ac.uk/181_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-https://eprints.soas.ac.uk/181-134">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the contribution made by the <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_UN_Peacekeeping_Force" title="Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force">Bangladesh UN Peacekeeping Force</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Civil_War" title="Sierra Leone Civil War">Sierra Leone Civil War</a> under the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Mission_in_Sierra_Leone" title="United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone">United Nations Mission in Sierra Leone</a>, the government of <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a> declared <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> an honorary official language in December 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <i>World Refugee Survey 2008</i>, published by the US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants, Sierra Leone had a population of 8,700 <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">refugees</a> and asylum seekers at the end of 2007. Nearly 20,000 Liberian refugees voluntarily returned to <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> over the course of 2007. Of the refugees remaining in Sierra Leone, nearly all were Liberian.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

      <p>The populations quoted above for the five largest cities are from the 2004 census. The figure for Freetown is for the Western Urban Area (Greater Freetown). Other figures are estimates from the source cited. Different sources give different estimates. Some claim that <a href="/wiki/Magburaka" title="Magburaka">Magburaka</a> should be included in the above list, but there is considerable difference among sources. One source estimates the population at 14,915,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> whilst another puts it as high as 85,313.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> "Pandebu-Tokpombu" is presumably the extended town of Torgbonbu, which had a population of 10,716 in the 2004 census. "Gbendembu" had a larger population of 12,139 in that census. In the 2004 census, Waterloo had a population of 34,079. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG/220px-Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG/330px-Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG/440px-Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3981" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pendemdu_Mosque_and_Church.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mosque and church in Sierra Leone
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sierra Leone is officially a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>. <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> are the two main religions in the country. The constitution of Sierra Leone provides for <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sierra_Leone" title="Government of Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone Government</a> generally protects it. The Sierra Leonean Government is constitutionally forbidden from establishing a <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, though Muslim and Christian prayers are usually held in the country at the beginning of major political occasions, including presidential inaugurations and the official opening of the new session of Parliament. </p>
      <p>Surveys of the religious make up of Sierra Leone vary widely, though <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> make up the majority of the population. Based on 2015 estimates of the population of Sierra Leone, 77% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, 22% are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, and 1% practise <a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">African traditional religion</a>. </p>
      <p>According to a 2010 estimates by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> 78% of Sierra Leone's population are <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>), 20.9 are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestants</a>) and 1% belong to a traditional African religion or other beliefs. The Inter-Religious Council of Sierra Leone estimated that 77% of Sierra Leone's population are Muslims, 21% are Christians, and 2% are followers of traditional African religion.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Most of Sierra Leone's ethnic groups are Muslim majority, including the country's two largest ethnic groups: the <a href="/wiki/Mende_people" title="Mende people">Mende</a> and <a href="/wiki/Temne_people" title="Temne people">Temne</a>. </p>
      <p>Sierra Leone is regarded as one of the most religiously tolerant countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="factual statement without mention of author (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Muslims and Christians collaborate and interact with each other peacefully. <a href="/wiki/Religious_violence" title="Religious violence">Religious violence</a> is very rare in the country. Even during the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leonean_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leonean Civil War">Sierra Leonean Civil War</a> people were never targeted because of their religion. </p>
      <p>The country is home to the Sierra Leone Inter-Religious Council, which is made up of both Christian and Muslim religious leaders to promote peace and tolerance throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The Islamic holidays of <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Maulid-un-Nabi</a> (Birthday of the <a href="/wiki/Prophets_and_messengers_in_Islam" title="Prophets and messengers in Islam">Islamic prophet</a> <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>) are observed as <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Public holidays in Sierra Leone">national holidays in Sierra Leone</a>. The Christian holidays of <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a> and <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a> are also <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Public holidays in Sierra Leone">national holidays in Sierra Leone</a>. In politics the overwhelming majority of Sierra Leoneans vote for a candidate without regard of the candidate being a Muslim or a Christian. All of Sierra Leone's Heads of State have been Christians except <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Tejan_Kabbah" title="Ahmad Tejan Kabbah">Ahmad Tejan Kabbah</a>, who was a Muslim. </p>
      <p>The overwhelming majority of Sierra Leonean Muslims, are adherent to the <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> tradition of Islam in practice. Most of the Mosques and Islamic schools across Sierra Leone are based in <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahmadiyya Muslims">Ahmadiyya Muslims</a> make up about 10% of the country's Muslim population. Sierra Leone has a vibrant Ahmaddiya Muslim population, especially in the southern city of <a href="/wiki/Bo,_Sierra_Leone" title="Bo, Sierra Leone">Bo</a>, that is home to a large Ahmadiyya Muslim population. There are five hundred Ahmaddiyya Mosque across Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a> does not have strong present in Sierra Leone, and there are virtually no <a href="/wiki/Shia_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Muslims">Shia Muslims</a> in the country. Most of Sierra Leonean Muslims of the Sunni and Ahmadiyya sect generally pray together in the same Mosque.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The vast majority of Sierra Leonean Muslims are adherent to the <a href="/wiki/Maliki_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Maliki school">Maliki school</a> of Sunni Islam. The Maliki school is by far the largest and most dominant Islamic school of jurisprudence across Sierra Leone. Many Ahmadiyya Muslims in Sierra Leone also follow the Maliki Jurisprudence. </p>
      <p>The Sierra Leone Islamic Supreme Council, is the highest Islamic religious organisation in Sierra Leone and is made up of the country's Imams, Islamic scholars, and other Islamic clerics across the country. Sheikh Muhammad Taha Jalloh is the president of the Sierra Leone Supreme Islamic Council.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> The United Council of Imams, is a very influential Islamic religious body in Sierra Leone, that is made up of all <a href="/wiki/Imams" class="mw-redirect" title="Imams">imams</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mosques" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosques">mosques</a> throughout Sierra Leone. The president of the United Council of Imam is Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Alhaji" class="mw-redirect" title="Alhaji">Alhaji</a> Muhammad Habib Sheriff.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The two largest <a href="/wiki/Mosques" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosques">mosques</a> in Sierra Leone are the <a href="/wiki/Freetown_Central_Mosque" title="Freetown Central Mosque">Freetown Central Mosque</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ghadafi_Central_Mosque&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ghadafi Central Mosque (page does not exist)">Ghadafi Central Mosque</a> (built by former <a href="/wiki/Libyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Libyan">Libyan</a> dictator <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>), both located in the capital <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>. </p>
      <p>The large majority of Sierra Leonean Christians are <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, of which the largest groups are the <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Wesleyan">Wesleyan</a> _ <a href="/wiki/Methodists" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodists">Methodists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Other Christian Protestant <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">denominations</a> with significant presence in the country include <a href="/wiki/Presbyterians" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterians">Presbyterians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The Council of Churches is the Christian religious organisation that is made up of <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches across Sierra Leone. Recently there has been an increase of <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> churches, especially in Freetown. </p>
      <p>In September 2017, a Sierra Leone-based Nigerian <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> Christian pastor name Victor Ajisafe was arrested by the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Police" title="Sierra Leone Police">Sierra Leone Police</a> and held in <a href="/wiki/Jail" class="mw-redirect" title="Jail">jail</a> after he made controversial remarks against <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and Sierra Leonean Muslims in particular at his church <a href="/wiki/Sermon" title="Sermon">sermon</a> in the capital <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>. Ajisafe was apparently angry after a <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwean" class="mw-redirect" title="Zimbabwean">Zimbabwean</a> Muslim <a href="/wiki/Cleric" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleric">cleric</a> <a href="/wiki/Mufti_Menk" class="mw-redirect" title="Mufti Menk">Mufti Menk</a> had visited Sierra Leone and preached to large crowds.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Many Christian organisations in Sierra Leone, including the Council of Churches condemned Ajisafe's sermon against Islam and Muslims. Ajisafe's church was temporarily shut down by the Sierra Leone government and his church licence was temporarily suspended too. The incident brought religious tension in Sierra Leone, in a country known for its very high level of religious tolerance, as many Sierra Leonean Muslims at home and abroad were extremely angry, many called for Ajisafe to be <a href="/wiki/Deported" class="mw-redirect" title="Deported">deported</a> back to his home country of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. The pastor while in Sierra Leone <a href="/wiki/Police_custody" class="mw-redirect" title="Police custody">police custody</a> apologised to Sierra Leonean Muslims and to the government of Sierra Leone. After several days in jail, Ajisafe was released, his church licence was given back to him, and his church was later reopened under strict government condition during several months of <a href="/wiki/Probation" title="Probation">probation</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nondenominational_Christianity" title="Nondenominational Christianity">Non-denominational Protestants</a> form a significant minority of Sierra Leone's Christian population.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> are the largest group of non-Protestant Christians in Sierra Leone, forming about 8% of Sierra Leone's population and 26% of the Christian population in Sierra Leone.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%E2%80%99s_Witnesses" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehovah’s Witnesses">Jehovah’s Witnesses</a><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> are the two most prominent <a href="/wiki/Nontrinitarianism" title="Nontrinitarianism">non Trinitarian</a> Christians in Sierra Leone, and they form a small but significant minority of the Christian population in Sierra Leone. A small community of <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christians">Orthodox Christians</a> resides in the capital Freetown.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sierra_Leone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Sierra_Leone" title="Ethnic groups in Sierra Leone">Ethnic groups in Sierra Leone</a>
      </div>
